## Just the way it is.” Trump says Canada’s prime minister can do nothing to reduce tariffs today

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/business/trump-carney-tariffs)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 12:26:00-20:26_

### Summary

President Donald Trump, during his first Oval Office meeting with Canadian Prime Minister Mark Carney, declared that there was nothing Carney could say to convince him to reduce tariffs on Canadian goods, stating, 'No, just the way it is.' Trump expressed his belief that Canada unfairly benefits the United States through subsidies and free military protection, among other advantages, despite official US statistics showing a 2024 goods and services trade deficit with Canada of $35.7 billion. Carney acknowledged that Canada benefits from trade with the US, but emphasized that negotiations for lower tariffs would take time and involve significant discussion. Trump remained open to potential negotiations but did not promise a quick resolution to the issue of tariffs.

### Key Takeaways
  - President Donald Trump refused to reduce tariffs on Canadian goods, stating they were 'Just the way it is,' despite complaints about unfair treatment from the previous administration.
  - There is a 2024 trade deficit of $35.7 billion with Canada, significantly less than the $200 billion claimed by the Trump administration.
  - Prime Minister Mark Carney acknowledged that both countries benefit from trade but suggested negotiations for lower tariffs to be conducted over time.

### Named Entities
- **Donald Trump**
    - The President of the United States who refused to reduce tariffs on Canadian goods.
    - He is the central figure who made the decision to not reduce tariffs, which is the main focus of the article.
- **Mark Carney**
    - The Prime Minister of Canada who was in meetings with Trump.
    - He represents Canada in the discussions and highlights the potential benefits of trade while emphasizing the complexities involved in negotiations.

### Summary

Another F/A-18 Super Hornet fighter jet from the USS Harry S. Truman aircraft carrier has been lost at sea, marking the second jet lost from the carrier in just over a week. The incident remains under investigation, but two of the people familiar with the matter believe an arrestment failure occurred during the jet's landing, causing the pilot and weapons systems officer to eject. The jet crashed into the sea and has not been recovered. Separately, the Iran-backed Houthi rebel group allegedly fired upon the Truman on Tuesday, despite an apparent ceasefire announced by President Trump. US Naval assets in the Red Sea have repeatedly faced Houthi attacks since November 2023, including the use of Phalanx Close-In Weapon System by a destroyer to defend against Houthi missile attacks. The USS Harry S. Truman, in particular, has experienced problems during its Red Sea deployment, including a collision with a merchant ship near Egypt in February and another F/A-18 jet being accidentally fired upon by another US destroyer in December.

## Two more judges block the Trump administration’s use of the Alien Enemies Act to deport migrants

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/politics/judge-blocks-trump-administration-deport-migrants)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 18:00:00-20:00_

### Summary

Two more federal judges have blocked the Trump administration's use of the Alien Enemies Act for deportations, emphasizing the constitutional protections and limitations on wartime powers for removal of migrants. District Judge Alvin Hellerstein in the Southern District of New York and Judge Charlotte Sweeney in Colorado ruled that the administration has exceeded its authority. These decisions come as the Trump administration has faced legal challenges to its rapid deportation practices, particularly those using the Alien Enemies Act to deport migrants from Venezuela. Both rulings state that the Alien Enemies Act should not be used for deportations and that the administration has not shown a need for a military invasion, which is a requirement for the use of this law. The rulings indicate the ongoing legal battles against the use of this wartime power to expedite deportations.

### Key Takeaways
  - Two more federal judges blocked the Trump administration’s use of the Alien Enemies Act to deport migrants on May 6, 2025.
  - Judge Alvin Hellerstein's ruling in New York prevented indefinite deportations under the Alien Enemies Act.
  - Judge Charlotte Sweeney's ruling in Colorado also blocked the use of the act for rapid deportations.
  - The Alien Enemies Act is being challenged on grounds that it violates constitutional protections and isn't being used legally.
  - The high court has yet to determine whether the act is being used legally, but appellate courts have limited the use of this law for deportation purposes.

### Named Entities
- **Alvin Hellerstein**
    - District Judge in the Southern District of New York, who ruled against the use of the Alien Enemies Act.
    - His ruling is a significant step in limiting the Trump administration's use of the Alien Enemies Act for deportations, as he blocked the administration from deporting migrants indefinitely under the act.
- **Charlotte Sweeney**
    - US District Judge in Colorado who issued a preliminary injunction blocking the president from using the Alien Enemies Act to deport migrants in Colorado.
    - Her decision adds to the legal challenges to the Trump administration's use of the Alien Enemies Act for rapid deportations, as she also blocked the president from using it in Colorado.
- **Kilmar Abrego Garcia**
    - A Maryland man who was illegally deported to El Salvador and sent to the notorious CECOT megaprison.
    - The case of Kilmar Abrego Garcia highlights the rapid and unauthorized deportations under the Trump administration, which has faced legal challenges in this case.

    - Venezuelan gang Tren de Aragua that the Trump administration used as a reason for deportations.
    - The gang is mentioned by both judges as a reason for deportations, highlighting the political motivations behind the use of the Alien Enemies Act for deportations.
- **Donald Trump**
    - The former President of the United States who initiated the use of the Alien Enemies Act for deportations.
    - His administration is the subject of these legal challenges, as the judges ruled against the use of the Alien Enemies Act under his presidency.
- **Joe Biden**
    - The former President of the United States who appointed Judge Charlotte Sweeney.
    - Biden appointed Judge Sweeney, highlighting the political context of the rulings against the use of the Alien Enemies Act under the Trump administration.

## The foods you pack in your kids’ lunch boxes may impact when they start menstruating, study suggests

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/health/nutrition-early-menstruation-wellness)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 17:50:00-20:50_

### Summary

A new study in the journal Human Reproduction indicates that a more inflammatory diet is associated with a 15% greater chance of a girl having her first menstrual cycle in the following month, while a healthier diet reduces this risk by 8%. The study, conducted on nearly 7,500 children aged 9 to 14, used the Alternative Healthy Eating Index and Empirical Dietary Inflammatory Pattern to measure the diets of participants. It found that the connection between diet and age at first menstruation was not solely influenced by body mass index (BMI). Key elements of a healthy diet, according to the study, include fruits, vegetables, healthy fats, whole grains, and nuts and legumes, while unhealthy or inflammatory diets include red and processed meats, refined grains, and sugar-sweetened beverages. The findings suggest that parents and caregivers should focus on promoting a healthy diet for their children, as it may influence long-term health outcomes. Dr. Holly Harris, the senior author of the study, notes that an early first period, which is impacted by both genetics and external factors, is associated with a higher risk of chronic conditions such as breast cancer, cardiovascular disease, and diabetes. She emphasizes the importance of access to healthy meal options and school-based meal guidelines to support this goal.

### Key Takeaways
  - Eating an inflammatory diet in late childhood and early adolescence is associated with a 15% greater chance of a girl having her first period in the next month, while a healthier diet reduces the risk by 8%.

### Named Entities
- **Fred Hutch Cancer Center**

    - The journal where the study was published.
    - This is where the research findings were shared and can be accessed by the public.

    - The name of the study from which the data was gathered.
    - The study data provides the basis for the research findings and impacts discussed in the article.

    - The senior study author and associate professor of epidemiology at Fred Hutch Cancer Center in Seattle.

## Divided Supreme Court allows Trump administration to begin enforcing ban on transgender service members

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/politics/supreme-court-ban-transgender-service-members)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 16:37:00-20:37_

### Summary

The U.S. Supreme Court has ruled that the Trump administration can immediately enforce a ban on transgender service members in the military. This decision follows legal challenges from various parties, including LGBTQ rights organizations. The ban prohibits individuals with gender dysphoria from serving and forbids transgender Americans from joining the military. The Supreme Court's decision was a victory for the Trump administration and their policies, but it was also met with opposition from legal challenges and concerns about the ban's impact on transgender service members' careers and readiness of the military. The Pentagon must process transgender service members for separation and not allow new transgender individuals to join. The decision is the result of ongoing legal battles and reflects the ongoing debate over the constitutionality of such policies.

### Key Takeaways
  - The Supreme Court allowed the Trump administration to begin immediately enforcing a ban on transgender service members in the military.
  - The ban prohibits service members with a current diagnosis or history of gender dysphoria from serving, and forbids transgender Americans from joining any branch of the military.
  - The decision is a victory for President Donald Trump's second-term agenda, which faces ongoing legal challenges from various parties.
  - The ban has been previously allowed by the Supreme Court during President Trump's first term, but was later reversed by President Joe Biden.
  - The Pentagon is required to process transgender service members for separation and is not allowed to allow transgender individuals to join the military.
  - There is uncertainty around the exact number of transgender individuals serving in the military, but it is believed to be around 14,000 in 2018.
  - The decision to enforce the ban comes after federal judges concluded that it violated constitutional rights of transgender Americans.
  - The administration argues the ban is necessary for the military's readiness, while those challenging it argue it is a violation of equal protection.
  - LGBTQ rights groups and legal challenges are concerned about the impact of the ban on transgender service members and the potential for their immediate discharge.

### Named Entities
- **Donald Trump**

    - The entity is relevant to the article because Settle's ruling was a significant part of the legal challenges to the ban, which the Supreme Court overturned.

    - Solicitor General who argued in favor of the administration's policies.
    - Sauer's argument was part of the defense of the ban, and the Supreme Court's decision partially followed his stance.

    - US District Judge who issued a preliminary injunction in the DC case.
    - Reyes' preliminary injunction is part of the ongoing legal battles and appeals related to the ban.

    - Transgender lieutenant in the Army who is the lead plaintiff in the DC case.
    - Talbott's perspective and concerns highlight the personal and professional impact of the ban on transgender service members.

    - LGBTQ rights organization that is part of the legal challenge against the ban.
    - Lambda Legal's involvement indicates the broader societal impact of the ban on transgender individuals.

    - LGBTQ rights organization that is part of the legal challenge against the ban.
    - Their involvement underscores the political and social significance of the issue.

    - Biden's role in reversing the ban shows the political and legal evolution of the transgender military service ban during his presidency.

## The quest to get REAL IDs before this week’s deadline leads to frustration for many

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/us/dmv-real-id-deadline-nj)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 19:41:00-20:41_

### Summary

The REAL ID deadline for people to obtain a REAL ID for air travel before May 7, 2025, has created significant challenges and frustrations for many Americans. Scott Case, a frequent business traveler from New Jersey, faced difficulties getting his REAL ID after the deadline, as the Department of Homeland Security has begun enforcement. Despite the fact that passengers without REAL IDs will still be allowed to fly, there are concerns about potential additional screening and steps they may have to take. The process of obtaining REAL IDs has been described as a challenge due to high demand and limited resources, with many states reporting significant demand for REAL IDs and staff working non-stop to assist as many eligible citizens as possible. As the deadline approaches, Americans are experiencing long lines and frustration, with some facing difficulties in getting their IDs, even with appointments set.

### Key Takeaways
  - Many Americans are facing difficulties in obtaining REAL IDs before the deadline, especially on the final few days before enforcement.

### Named Entities
- **Scott Case**
    - A frequent business traveler from Collingswood, New Jersey who realized the REAL ID deadline was coming up and decided to head to his local DMV on Monday.
    - Scott Case's experience highlights the frustrations and challenges many Americans are facing as they rush to comply with the new REAL ID requirement before the deadline.
- **REAL ID Act**
    - Congress passed the REAL ID Act in 2005 as a way to enhance security for identification.
    - The REAL ID Act is the root of the issue, as it requires new minimum standards for state-issued driver’s licenses and IDs to improve security, but it has created challenges for people trying to obtain REAL IDs.
- **Department of Homeland Security**
    - The U.S. agency that will enforce the REAL ID regulations starting May 7.

## T. rex ancestors likely crossed land bridge from Asia to North America 70 million years ago, study finds

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/science/t-rex-ancestors-asia-study-scli-intl)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 19:36:00.000Z_

### Summary

A study led by Cassius Morrison, a doctoral student at University College London, suggests that T. rex's direct ancestors crossed from Asia to North America via a land bridge around 70 million years ago, arriving after the formation of the Bering Strait. The team used mathematical modeling and data from the fossil record to conclude that T. rex is more closely related to Tarbosaurus in Asia than to large predators in North America like Daspletosaurus. According to the study, T. rex experienced a rapid increase in size during a time of falling global temperatures, likely due to cooler climates, which provided opportunities for the dinosaur to grow and become a dominant predator. The study's findings highlight the influence of climate change on the evolution of T. rex and its dominance during the Cretaceous period.

### Key Takeaways
  - T. rex's direct ancestors crossed from Asia to North America via a land bridge around 70 million years ago.
  - The study's findings suggest that T. rex likely evolved into its giant size in response to cooler climate conditions.
  - T. rex was more closely related to Tarbosaurus in Asia compared to top predators in North America.
  - The study used mathematical modeling and data from the fossil record to support its conclusions.
  - The extinction of another group of giant meat-eating dinosaurs allowed T. rex to occupy the top of the food chain and grow to its enormous size.

### Named Entities
- **T. rex**
    - The name of a famous large carnivorous dinosaur from the Cretaceous period, the subject of the study.
    - The entity at the center of the study's findings, providing context and interest for the public and researchers.
- **Tyrannosaurids**
    - A group of meat-eating dinosaurs, including T. rex, that the study focuses on.
    - The subject of the study, helping to understand the origins and evolution of T. rex.
- **Cassius Morrison**
    - A doctoral student at University College London leading the study.
    - The primary researcher responsible for the study findings, providing credibility to the research.
- **Steve Brusatte**
    - A paleontologist at the University of Edinburgh who was not involved in the study.
    - The expert who reviewed the study and provided commentary, offering additional insight on the subject matter.
- **Tyrannosaurs**
    - A group of large meat-eating dinosaurs, including T. rex, that the study tracks.
    - The subject of the study's research, providing context for the evolution and size of T. rex.
- **Carcharodontosaurids**
    - Another group of large meat-eating dinosaurs, which went extinct, providing the ecological space for T. rex to grow to enormous size.
    - The group that went extinct, helping to explain the growth and dominance of T. rex, as they were the top predators before its emergence.

### Important Dates
  - **2025-05-06**
    - The date when the study was published and made public.
  - **7000-01-01**
    - The approximate date when the land bridge connecting Asia and North America formed, allowing the T. rex ancestors to cross over.

### Important Timeframes
  - **From _2025-05-06_ to _2025-05-06_**
    - The time frame when the study's findings were published and can be accessed.
  - **From _7000-01-01_ to _7000-01-01_**
    - The time frame when the land bridge allowing T. rex ancestors to cross from Asia to North America was formed.

### Summary

WeightWatchers, a 62-year-old program that revolutionized dieting for millions of people, filed for bankruptcy. The company, now known as WW International, entered Chapter 11 in response to over $1.5 billion in debt and a failing business strategy that has not kept pace with more convenient weight loss options. CEO Tara Comonte stated that the bankruptcy process would provide the company with the flexibility to accelerate innovation, reinvest in its members, and lead in the rapidly evolving weight management landscape. The filing follows a failed turnaround plan from former CEO Sima Sistani, who bought a telehealth platform that connected patients with doctors for weight-loss and diabetes drugs, and the departure of star investor Oprah Winfrey from the board. WW's history is tied to Jean Nidetch, who founded the company in 1963 with a philosophy of using an emotional approach to dieting and exercise.

### Key Takeaways
  - WeightWatchers, a 62-year-old dieting program, has filed for bankruptcy

## Inside the multi-day meltdown at Newark airport

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/us/inside-the-multi-day-meltdown-at-newark-airport)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 19:10:00-20:10_

### Summary

A multi-day air traffic control meltdown at Newark Liberty International Airport in New Jersey resulted from a failure of copper wiring that transmits information between the FAA's radar facility in Westbury, New York, and Newark's control center. The outage impacted flights arriving at and departing from the airport, causing delays, cancellations, and cancellations exceeding 4 hours for some passengers. The incident highlighted the challenges of an outdated air traffic control system, contributing to staffing shortages and equipment failures, and compounded by the loss of radar and communication capabilities. Controllers were left to manage flights with only backup communication systems, leading to anxiety and trauma. United Airlines preemptively canceled 35 round trip flights to and from Newark to assist passengers. The U.S. Department of Transportation plans to overhaul the air traffic control system, aiming for a 'state-of-the-art' system to be in place in three to four years. However, Peter Goelz, a former safety board director, expressed concern about the safety implications, stating that the airport might not be safe for the next ten days due to the ongoing issues.

### Key Takeaways
  - Air traffic control systems experienced a failure that resulted in a weeklong outage at Newark Liberty International Airport, causing delays and cancellations for thousands of passengers.
  - The outage began with communication and radar failure at an FAA facility in Westbury, New York, and was compounded by staffing shortages and equipment issues.
  - The incident highlighted the challenges of an outdated air traffic control system, which contributed to ongoing delays at the airport.
  - The FAA acknowledged the shortage of air traffic controllers, a critical role during such disruptions, and noted that the system is under strain due to both understaffing and outdated technology.
  - The U.S. Department of Transportation is planning a significant overhaul of the air traffic control system, aiming to make it more modern and capable of handling current demands.
  - The incident has raised concerns about the safety and reliability of air traffic control systems, leading to public scrutiny and potential calls for action.
  - The Newark airport incident is part of a broader context of aviation challenges and safety concerns that have been recurring over the past few years.

### Named Entities
- **FAA**
    - Federal Aviation Administration, the agency responsible for the air traffic control system.
    - The FAA is directly responsible for the air traffic control system that experienced the failure, making it a central subject of the article and the focus of discussions about the incident.
- **Newark Liberty International Airport**
    - A major U.S. airport where the air traffic control system failure impacted flight operations.
    - The airport is the primary location where the incident took place and the primary focus of the delays and cancellations reported in the article.
- **United Airlines**
    - An airline affected by the air traffic control system failure, reporting delays and cancellations.
    - United Airlines is a major player in the aviation industry and provided information on their response to the incident, including the cancellation of flights and providing customer assistance.
- **United States Department of Transportation**
    - The government agency responsible for overseeing the air traffic control system and planning improvements.
    - The Department of Transportation is involved in the planned overhaul of the air traffic control system, demonstrating the federal government’s response to the incident's consequences.
- **National Air Traffic Controllers Association**
    - A union representing air traffic controllers.
    - The union is mentioned in relation to the air traffic controllers’ response to the incident, including their concerns about staffing shortages and the psychological impact of the event.
- **Peter Goelz**
    - A former managing director of the National Transportation Safety Board.
    - Goelz's opinion on the incident and the impact on safety contributes to the broader context of the article's discussion on the consequences of the failure.

    - 'The date when air traffic control issues first occurred, marking the beginning of the incident that led to the weeklong outage and subsequent delays at Newark airport.

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/politics/us-to-stop-strikes-on-houthis-in-yemen)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 18:48:00-20:48_

### Summary

President Donald Trump announced on May 6, 2025, that the United States would cease military strikes against the Iran-backed Houthi rebels in Yemen. This decision was made in response to the Houthi rebels' statement that they no longer wish to engage in hostilities. The ceasefire, facilitated by Oman, aims to create a momentum for the ongoing US-Iran nuclear deal negotiations. While the ceasefire is expected to aid the US in its negotiations with Iran, it is unclear how it will impact Israel's ongoing operations against the Houthi rebels, who have fired missiles at Israel. The U.S. did not inform Israel about the ceasefire before announcing it in the Oval Office, which caused a significant reaction in the Israeli government.

### Key Takeaways
  - President Donald Trump announced a ceasefire with the Houthi rebels in Yemen, ending the U.S. military strikes against the group following their acknowledgment that they do not want to fight anymore. This ceasefire aims to facilitate nuclear deal talks with Iran and build momentum for negotiations.
  - The ceasefire comes after recent diplomatic efforts and communications between the U.S., Oman, and the Houthi rebels, with Oman stating that a ceasefire agreement has been reached between the two sides.
  - The ceasefire is expected to serve as a stepping stone for US-Iran nuclear negotiations, as the U.S. special envoy has been working to broker a ceasefire with the Houthi rebels over the last week.
  - The decision to end the strikes against the Houthi rebels in Yemen comes amid ongoing tensions with Israel, with the Houthi leaders stating that the ceasefire will only be evaluated on the ground, and they will continue their aggression against Israel until its military offensive in Gaza stops.
  - It is unclear how the ceasefire will impact Israeli military operations in Yemen, given that Israel has been carrying out days of escalating fighting with the Houthi rebels and has carried out multiple strikes against their targets.
  - The U.S. did not inform Israel about its de facto truce with the Houthis before Trump announced it in the Oval Office, which caused a significant shock for Israeli officials.

Both leaders spoke for about 95% of the meeting time, with Trump dominating the conversation, and the topics discussed included the Middle East, Barack Obama's presidential library, high-speed rail in California, and Canada's sovereignty. Despite the contentious tone, the meeting was relatively mild compared to previous confrontations. Trump's remarks about Canada's dependence on the United States and his public criticism on Truth Social were notable, though the two leaders agreed to meet again at the G7 summit. ## Two United Airlines planes clip wings while preparing to depart San Francisco International Airport

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/us/san-francisco-united-airlines-plane)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 17:17:00-20:17_

### Summary

Two United Airlines planes clipped wings while preparing to depart San Francisco International Airport on Tuesday, as per the Federal Aviation Administration. This incident is the second of its kind in less than a month, emphasizing the recurrence of similar incidents. No injuries occurred and passengers were able to deplane normally. The Federal Aviation Administration is investigating the incidents, seeking to understand and mitigate the risks associated with wingtip strikes at airports. The San Francisco incident, involving United Airlines Flight 863 and United Flight 877, highlights the potential for future occurrences and the need for immediate action. The incidents have also occurred at Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport, with an earlier incident involving two American Airlines regional jets, further emphasizing the recurring nature of such incidents and the need for improved airport safety and communication systems.

## FDA chooses Dr. Vinay Prasad to lead biologics, vaccines division

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/health/fda-vinay-prasad-vaccines)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 17:53:00-20:53_

### Summary

The US Food and Drug Administration (FDA) has appointed Dr. Vinay Prasad, a hematologist and oncologist, to lead its Center for Biologics Evaluation and Research, the division that oversees vaccines and biologic medicines. Dr. Prasad, a professor at the University of California San Francisco, succeeded Dr. Peter Marks, who had been leading the division for 13 years. Marks resigned in March due to disagreements with the FDA's response to the COVID-19 pandemic, particularly regarding vaccine safety. Dr. Prasad has previously criticized the FDA's Warp Speed effort and vaccine recommendations, particularly those for children. His appointment comes amid discussions about imposing new requirements for future vaccines and has led to concerns from biotech companies and the stock market. Dr. Prasad's background in oncology and his stance on vaccine safety have made him a critical figure in the FDA's oversight of vaccines and biologic medicines.

### Key Takeaways

## Lawmakers want answers after reporting reveals crippling vacancies at hurricane-prone National Weather Service office

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/weather/national-weather-service-staffing-hurricane-houston)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 16:18:00-20:18_

### Summary

Three Houston-area Democratic Representatives have sent a letter to the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration's acting head, Laura Grimm, highlighting the alarming staffing shortages at the National Weather Service's Houston-Galveston office just as hurricane season is about to begin. The letter points out that all management positions are currently vacant, including the meteorologist-in-charge, and that experienced meteorologists have been laid off, bought out, or retired. This has left the office under-resourced and at risk of failing to provide essential weather forecasts and warnings. The letter requests details on the timeline for filling these positions, as the agency is facing the possibility of reduced 24/7 operations if the problem isn't addressed promptly. This situation is particularly serious as Houston is one of 30 NWS forecast offices experiencing a severe lack of experienced meteorologists, a problem compounded by layoffs under the Trump administration.

### Key Takeaways
  - Three House Democrats have sent a letter to NOAA's acting head, expressing concerns about the staffing shortages at the National Weather Service's Houston-Galveston office, especially the vacancies in management positions and the loss of experienced meteorologists just before hurricane season.

## US is shutting down Office of Palestinian Affairs and merging it into its embassy in Jerusalem

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/politics/us-shutting-down-office-of-palestinian-affairs)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 16:14:00-20:14_

### Summary

US Secretary of State Marco Rubio announced the closure of the Office of Palestinian Affairs and its merger into the US embassy in Jerusalem. State Department spokesperson Tammy Bruce explained that this move aims to restore the unified US diplomatic mission that reports directly to the US ambassador to Israel, Mike Huckabee. The closure is claimed not to reflect any outreach to Palestinians or Gaza. This decision appears to be a step in sidelining Palestinian engagement with the US government, especially through the new Bureau. The announcement coincides with Israel's approval to expand its war in Gaza and comes after the first Trump administration shuttered the consulate general and closed its lines of communication with Palestinians. The Biden administration did not reopen the consulate general, which gave the Palestinian Authority a dedicated US representative and direct line to Washington. This move is seen as a further downgrading of US-Palestinian relations, especially amid the ongoing conflict in Gaza and Trump's earlier rhetoric about being good to Gaza.

### Key Takeaways
  - US is shutting down the Office of Palestinian Affairs and merging it into the US embassy in Jerusalem.
  - This move is a further downgrading of relations with the Palestinian people.
  - The decision is attributed to US Secretary of State Marco Rubio and will be implemented by Ambassador Mike Huckabee.
  - It is claimed that the move does not reflect any commitment to outreach to the Palestinian people or to the Gaza Strip.
  - The announcement comes after Israel approved plans to expand its war in Gaza, raising further concerns about US-Palestinian relations.

### Named Entities

    - State Department spokesperson who clarified the decision.

    - The person who will implement the merger decision.
    - This entity is important because he will be the one executing the changes that Rubio has decided upon.

    - Israeli Prime Minister who approved plans to expand war in Gaza.
    - This entity is relevant as his actions and statements suggest a shift in Israel's stance regarding Palestinians, which could affect US-Palestinian relations.

    - Israeli Far-right Finance Minister who advocated for the expansion of war in Gaza.
    - His statements are part of the context that underscores the severity of the situation for Palestinians.

    - Trump's first ambassador to Israel who closed the consulate.

- **Trump**
    - US President who originally closed the consulate.
    - His statement about needing to be good to Gaza is juxtaposed with the current decision to close the office, indicating a potential shift in US policy.

## First boats carrying Chinese goods with 145% tariffs are arriving in LA. Shipments are cut in half. Expect shortages soon

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/business/tariffs-price-increases-shortages-ports)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 16:14:00-20:14_

### Summary

The imposition of tariffs by President Donald Trump on most Chinese imports has resulted in a dramatic drop in the volume of imports from China. This reduction in imports has caused shortages and price hikes for American consumers, particularly in goods that have been subject to the 145% tariff. The Port of Los Angeles has reported a 50% decrease in imports from China, and many retailers and importers have canceled orders or are storing their goods in Chinese warehouses to avoid the tariffs. The National Retail Federation predicts a 20% year-over-year decline in imports, while JP Morgan expects a 75% to 80% drop from China itself. Economists at Wells Fargo also predict that imports will continue to decline, with a decline of at least 20% year-over-year. This situation is expected to continue as more ships with goods subject to tariffs are expected to arrive in the coming weeks.

### Key Takeaways
  - Shipments of Chinese goods to the US have been cut in half since the imposition of tariffs, causing shortages and price hikes for American consumers.
  - Imports from China are expected to fall by at least 20% year-over-year, with a 75% to 80% drop expected from China itself.
  - Businesses and retailers are paying more to store their products in Chinese warehouses rather than pay the tariffs and import from China.
  - The trade war has disrupted supply chains, leading to stockpiling and then stockpiles running out, leading to shortages and higher prices for goods.
  - Consumers may experience price hikes and shortages of certain items as the tariffs take full effect.
  - The situation is expected to continue as more ships with tariffs on Chinese goods are expected to arrive in the coming weeks.

### Named Entities
- **Gene Seroka**
    - Executive Director of the Port of Los Angeles who provided information about the decrease in imports from China due to tariffs.
    - He is providing critical information about the reduction in Chinese imports, which is central to the article's focus on the trade war and tariffs imposed by the Trump administration.
- **Ryan Petersen**
    - CEO of Flexport, a logistics and freight forwarding broker, who discussed the impact of tariffs on importers and retailers.
    - He highlights the significant impact of tariffs on the logistics industry, emphasizing that retailers and importers are unwilling to pay the steep cost and are canceling orders.
- **JP Morgan**
    - A financial institution that expected a 75% to 80% drop in imports from China.
    - They provide expected data on the decrease in imports from China, aligning with other sources in the article.
- **National Retail Federation**
    - A trade association representing retailers, which expects a 20% year-over-year decline in imports.
    - They provide expected data on the impact of tariffs on retail industry, aligning with the article's focus on consumer prices and shortages.
- **Wells Fargo economists**
    - Economists who wrote a note to investors predicting a decline in trade due to tariffs.
    - They provide expert analysis on the impact of tariffs on trade, aligning with the article's focus on the trade war and its economic effects.
- **Daniel Vielhaber**

## Civil rights lawsuit filed in Florida deputy’s killing of US Airman Roger Fortson

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/us/us-airman-roger-fortson-shot-lawsuit)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 16:14:00-20:14_

### Summary

A civil rights lawsuit has been filed in Florida on behalf of the family of a fatal shooting victim, Senior Airman Roger Fortson, by a Florida sheriff's deputy, Eddie Duran. The complaint alleges that Deputy Duran used excessive and unconstitutional deadly force when he shot Fortson just seconds after the Black 23-year-old opened his apartment door on May 3, 2024. Fortson’s family is represented by Ben Crump, a civil rights attorney who has been involved in a number of cases involving law enforcement killings of Black people, including those of Michael Brown, Breonna Taylor, Tyre Nichols, and George Floyd. Duran has pleaded not guilty to a charge of manslaughter with a firearm. The complaint also details alleged failures by the Okaloosa County Sheriff’s Office in training and supervision and claims staff at the apartment complex where Fortson lived provided misleading information that led to the fatal law enforcement response. Fortson, who was assigned to the 4th Special Operations Squadron at Hurlburt Field, was alone at the time, talking with his girlfriend on a FaceTime video call. Only then did the deputy yell, 'Drop the gun!'

### Key Takeaways

The footage shows Patel attempting to grab the child from the mother's lap while on a scooter. Patel's lawyer argued that Patel was trying to prevent the child from falling, and presented evidence of his strong ties to the community, including property ownership, family, and involvement in local organizations. The prosecution argued that Patel was trying to take the child and fled after the incident. The judge ruled that Patel's bonds were appropriate, given the evidence and his community ties, and released him from jail.

Nebraska Republican Rep. The bill, authored by Georgia Republican Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, aims to require federal agencies to use the new name in all maps and documents. Despite the bill's potential to gain momentum, Bacon's opposition, along with that of Reps. Glenn Grothman and Jay Obernolte, complicates the legislation and reduces its chances of passing, as few, if any, Democrats are expected to support it. The White House has also weighed in on the issue, with the AP stating it will continue using the name 'Gulf of Mexico' in its coverage and stylebook, despite recognizing the new 'Gulf of America' name.

## Ukrainian drones attack Moscow, temporarily halting flights ahead of major military parade

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/europe/ukraine-drones-moscow-may-9-xi-intl-hnk)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 17:37:00-07:00_

### Summary

Ukrainian drones attacked Moscow for the second consecutive night, causing temporary flight suspensions and halting several airports' operations ahead of the upcoming Victory Day military parade in Russia. This incident highlights the ongoing conflict between Ukraine and Russia and the international response to the escalation. Moscow Mayor Sergey Sobyanin reported at least 19 Ukrainian drones were destroyed, one of which was near the city the previous night. Despite no immediate reports of serious damage or casualties, debris from downed drones fell on a major highway. Russia's defense ministry reported intercepting 105 Ukrainian drones overnight. The latest attack comes amid a major military parade expected to feature 29 leaders, including China's Xi Jinping. Kyiv warned against foreign participation in the parade, citing the desecration of the memory of the victory over Nazism. Meanwhile, Russia’s defense ministry canceled the Victory Parade in Crimea and Krasnador due to an air threat announced almost every night, adding to the complexity of the conflict. The Ukrainian military has demonstrated its technological advancements, including the recent shooting down of a Russian Su-30 fighter jet using a seaborne drone, further complicating the ongoing conflict and ceasefire negotiations between Ukraine and Russia.

### Key Takeaways
  - Ukrainian drones attacked Moscow, temporarily halting flights at four airports in the Russian capital and nine further afield ahead of a major military parade.
  - Ukraine called on international allies not to send troops to Russia’s Victory Day celebrations, warning that participation would amount to desecration of the memory of the victory over Nazism.
  - Victory Day is the most significant day in Russian President Vladimir Putin’s calendar, as he has long used it to rally public support and demonstrate the country’s military prowess.
  - Victory Day celebrations in parts of Russia, such as Crimea and Krasnador, have been canceled due to an air threat announced almost every night.
  - Ukraine has increasingly turned to drones to level the playing field with Russia, which boasts superior manpower and resources.
  - Russia and Ukraine have largely stalled in negotiations for a permanent ceasefire, with Ukraine demanding longer truces and Russia accusing Ukraine of continuing the war.
  - Kyiv has claimed it shot down a Russian Su-30 fighter jet in the Black Sea using a seaborne drone for the first time, showcasing its technological advancements in the conflict.

The appointment is seen as an attempt to address the country's economic and security challenges, such as the influence of the Trump administration and the push for increased defense spending. However, Merz's tenure is complicated by the political uncertainty, the influence of the far-right AfD party, and the potential for disruption within the new government. The appointment also highlights the complex political situation in Germany, with Merz facing challenges from both within his coalition and the increasing pressure from the AfD party.

## Trump admin plans to shut down money-saving Energy Star program soon, sources say

- [source](https://lite.cnn.com/2025/05/06/climate/energy-star-trump)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 15:21:00-20:21_

### Summary

The Trump administration is planning to shut down two key divisions within the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) focused on climate change and energy efficiency, including its consumer-facing Energy Star program. The EPA is planning to close its climate change division and climate protection partnership division, as well as its Energy Star program. This program, which launched by the Bush administration in 1992, is recognized by over 90% of US households and helps consumers find energy-efficient appliances. The changes are part of broader EPA organizational improvements and will impact several climate programs and reduce government measurements of fossil fuel emissions. Senate Appropriations Chair Susan Collins, a Republican from Maine, expressed confusion and concern over the Trump administration's decision to cut the Energy Star program. The program's elimination would contradict the administration's promise to reduce household energy costs, according to Paula Glover, president of the Alliance to Save Energy. However, the program's supporters argue that it has a significant return on investment, with every federal dollar invested in it yielding $350 in benefits. The Energy Star program helps consumers make informed decisions about energy-efficient appliances and is nearly universally supported by manufacturers, retailers, and consumers. The future of the program's certifications for appliances is not clear, as the EPA spokesperson did not respond to questions about their continuation.

### Key Takeaways
  - The Trump administration is planning to shut down two key Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) divisions focused on climate change and energy efficiency, including its consumer-facing Energy Star program.

### Named Entities
- **EPA**
    - The Environmental Protection Agency, a federal agency responsible for protecting human health and the environment.

    - A program implemented by the EPA that certifies energy-efficient appliances and helps consumers find cost-effective energy-efficient products.
    - Energy Star is one of the main entities to be affected by the planned changes, making it a central entity in the article.

    - President of the nonprofit coalition Alliance to Save Energy, which has called for the administration to save the program.
    - Glover's statement highlights the potential consequences of the planned elimination of Energy Star.
- **Susan Collins**
    - A Republican senator from Maine who has expressed concerns over the plan to shut down the program.
    - Collins's statement indicates the broader public and political concern over the program's future.
- **Joe Goffman**
    - A former EPA official who led the Office of Air and Radiation under Biden, and who has acknowledged the widespread support for Energy Star.

    - EPA Administrator under the Trump administration, who announced in March the agency's plans to roll back pollution rules.
    - Zeldin's actions in the Trump administration are linked to the current plans to shut down Energy Star, indicating a continuity of policy.

## What is happening at Newark Airport? This and other questions answered

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5388404)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 15:37:00-20:37_

### Summary

The article discusses the disruption at Newark Liberty International Airport, which has caused numerous flight delays and cancellations due to multiple issues such as air traffic controller staffing shortages, aging technology, bad weather, and the closure of one of the airport's busiest runways. The Federal Aviation Administration and the Transportation Department are working on plans to modernize and improve the air traffic control system, addressing the staffing shortage and other technological and procedural issues. Passengers are advised to check airline websites for travel advisories, plan ahead, and consider alternative routes if they need to connect through Newark. Senator Chuck Schumer called for an Inspector General investigation into the cause of issues at Newark Airport, highlighting the severity and scale of the problems at the airport.

### Key Takeaways
  - There have been multiple issues at Newark Liberty International Airport causing flight delays and cancellations, including a communication outage for air traffic controllers, runway closure for Newark's busiest runway, and a shortage of air traffic controllers.
  - The Federal Aviation Administration and the Transportation Department are working on plans to modernize and improve the air traffic control system, addressing the staffing shortage and other technological and procedural issues.
  - Passengers are advised to check airline websites for travel advisories, plan ahead, and consider alternative routes if they need to connect through Newark.

### Named Entities
- **Chuck Schumer**
    - U.S. Senate's top Democrat who called for an Inspector General investigation.
    - His call for an investigation highlights the severity and scale of the issues at Newark, prompting the need for government action to address the situation.

    - A flight tracking website.
    - It provides real-time data on flight delays and cancellations, allowing the public to understand the scope and scale of the disruption.
- **FAA**
    - Federal Aviation Administration, responsible for the nation's air traffic control.
    - They have been working on plans to address the issues, including staffing shortages, and have announced a new recruitment and retention incentive program.
- **National Air Traffic Controllers Association**
    - The union representing air traffic controllers.
    - They shared details about the communication blackout with the public and the FAA, helping to bring attention to the issue.
- **Newark Liberty International Airport**
    - The major hub airport experiencing issues.
    - It is the primary location of the flight delays and cancellations, and the focal point of the public's attention and concern.
- **National Transportation Safety Board (NTSB)**
    - The agency responsible for investigating aviation accidents.
    - Their investigation into the January 29 midair collision between a U.S. Army Black Hawk helicopter and an American Airlines regional jet, which led to 67 deaths, could potentially shed light on the role of air traffic controllers in the incident.
- **Transportation Secretary Sean Duffy**
    - The current U.S. Secretary of Transportation.
    - He has announced a new recruitment award and retention incentive program to boost hiring of controllers, addressing the staffing shortage at Newark and potentially nationwide.

    - This is when the incident of air traffic controller communication blackout occurred, highlighting a critical moment in the disruption at Newark Liberty International Airport.

## How archaic tech, staff shortages and construction made a meltdown at Newark Airport

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5388438)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 20:09:00-20:09_

### Summary

Hundreds of flights were delayed and cancelled at Newark Liberty International Airport on Tuesday due to bad weather, staffing shortages, outdated infrastructure, and the airport's busiest runway being closed for renovations. The Newark Airport incident on April 28, 2025, highlighted the need for modernizing the air traffic control system, especially with regards to outdated technology. There have been decades of issues and warnings regarding the need to update the air traffic control system, but funding constraints due to government shutdowns have hindered progress. Transportation Secretary Sean Duffy is expected to announce a major overhaul of U.S. air traffic control on May 8, targeting outdated infrastructure. The incident at Newark Airport serves as a case study for the broader challenges facing the U.S. air traffic control system, including staffing shortages, outdated technology, and infrastructure problems.

### Key Takeaways
  - Hundreds of flights were delayed and cancelled at Newark Liberty International Airport on Tuesday due to bad weather, staffing shortages, outdated infrastructure, and the airport's busiest runway being closed for renovations.
  - A major overhaul of U.S. air traffic control is expected to be announced by Transportation Secretary Sean Duffy on May 8, targeting outdated infrastructure.
  - The Newark Airport incident on April 28, 2025, highlighted the importance of modernizing the air traffic control system, especially with regards to outdated technology.
  - There have been decades of issues and warnings regarding the need to update the air traffic control system, but funding constraints due to government shutdowns have hindered progress.
  - The air traffic control system is described as archaic, with many systems still using technology from the late 1980s to the 1990s, including paper strips and floppy disks for data updates.

### Named Entities
- **Paul Rinaldi**
    - A former air traffic controller and vice president of safety and operations at Airlines for America who spoke with NPR.
    - Paul Rinaldi provides insights into the issues surrounding the Newark Airport incident and the need for modernizing the air traffic control system.
- **Airlines for America**
    - A trade group that lobbies on behalf of airlines.
    - Airlines for America, represented by Paul Rinaldi, provides a perspective on the challenges faced by the air traffic control system and the need for modernization.
- **Sean Duffy**
    - Transportation Secretary who is expected to announce a major overhaul of U.S. air traffic control.

Kennedy, Jr.

## 3 former Memphis police officers found not guilty in the death of Tyre Nichols

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5388488)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 16:16:00-04:00_

### Summary

A jury found three former Memphis, Tennessee police officers, Tadarrius Bean, Demetrius Haley, and Justin Smith, not guilty of all charges in the 2023 death of Tyre Nichols, including the most serious charge of second-degree murder. The officers were initially fired and charged with both federal and state crimes related to Nichols' death. Nichols, a 29-year-old father, was fatally beaten during a traffic stop in January 2023. Graphic video footage and other evidence showed the officers using excessive force against Nichols, including pepper spraying and using a stun gun. Despite the prosecution's claims that the officers used excessive force and failed to provide medical assistance, the defense argued that Nichols' death was due to his own aggressive behavior and the actions of another officer, Emmitt Martin, who repeatedly kicked and punched Nichols. The case is ongoing, with Nichols' family planning to sue the city of Memphis for $550 million. This verdict is part of the second trial for the officers, following their conviction in a previous federal case for witness tampering. The Nichols case has become a focal point in discussions about police reform in Memphis and the broader debate over policing and accountability.

### Key Takeaways
  - Three former Memphis police officers, Tadarrius Bean, Demetrius Haley, and Justin Smith, were found not guilty of all charges in the death of Tyre Nichols, a 29-year-old father who died in 2023.

- **Tyre Nichols**
    - The victim of the fatal beating by Memphis police officers.

    - One of the three officers found not guilty in the case of Tyre Nichols' death.
    - 'Bean is one of the three officers whose guilt was disputed, and his not guilty verdict highlights the complexity of the legal case.
- **Demetrius Haley**
    - One of the three officers found not guilty in the case of Tyre Nichols' death.
    - 'Haley is one of the three officers whose guilt was disputed, and his not guilty verdict adds to the controversy surrounding the case.
- **Justin Smith**
    - One of the three officers found not guilty in the case of Tyre Nichols' death.
    - 'Smith is one of the three officers whose guilt was disputed, and his not guilty verdict further complicates the legal proceedings.
- **RowVaughn Wells**
    - Mother of Tyre Nichols.
    - 'Wells' role as Nichols' mother is highlighted as she spoke briefly with the district attorney after the verdict, indicating her personal connection to the case.
- **Shelby County District Attorney**
    - Steve Mulroy, who represents the state in the case.
    - 'Steve Mulroy, representing the state, expressed 'devastation' and 'outrage' at the verdict, emphasizing his perspective on the case.

## After an Arizona man was shot, an AI video of him addresses his killer in court

- [source](https://text.npr.org/g-s1-64640)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 15:37:00.000Z_

### Summary

Stacey Wales, the sister of Christopher Pelkey, who was killed in a road rage incident in Chandler, Arizona, used artificial intelligence to create an AI-generated video of her brother's voice addressing his shooter at a sentencing hearing. Wales, who struggled to find the right words for a victim impact statement, turned to AI to create an authentic representation of her brother's voice. The AI avatar, named Chris, thanked those in Pelkey's life, including those who testified about him, and specifically addressed the shooter, Gabriel Paul Horcasitas, offering forgiveness. The video was presented during the sentencing hearing and received a positive response from the judge, Todd Lang. AI experts believe this is the first time such a technology has been used in court in the U.S. for a victim impact statement. The use of AI in court raises various legal and ethical questions, including consent, fairness, and whether the content was made in good faith.

### Key Takeaways
  - An AI-generated video of Christopher Pelkey addressed his shooter in court, likely the first time such a technology was used in the U.S. during a sentencing hearing.

### Named Entities
- **Stacey Wales**
    - A sister who was seeking a victim impact statement at the sentencing hearing for the man who killed her brother.
    - Stacey Wales is the central figure who used AI to create an AI avatar to address the shooter in court, making her the most relevant named entity in this case.
- **Christopher Pelkey**
    - The deceased brother of Stacey Wales who was killed in a road rage incident and whose voice was used in the AI-generated video.
    - Christopher Pelkey's voice was the source of the AI-generated video used in the court proceedings, making him a critical figure.
- **Gabriel Paul Horcasitas**
    - The shooter who killed Christopher Pelkey, and whose presence and reaction to the AI-generated video are part of the article's focus.
    - Horcasitas was the primary recipient of the AI-generated video, making him a significant named entity in the article.
- **Michael Cohen**
    - 'Former lawyer for President Trump who inadvertently sent AI-generated legal citations to his attorney.
    - Michael Cohen's incident is used to highlight the growing trend of AI usage in legal contexts, including the use of AI in court.
- **Todd Lang**
    - The judge presiding over the sentencing hearing where the AI-generated video was presented.
    - Judge Lang's reaction to the AI-generated video was a significant aspect of the article, as his comments on its impact were noted.
- **Maura Grossman**
    - A professor at the University of Waterloo who has studied the applications of AI in criminal and civil cases.
    - Maura Grossman's opinions on the use of AI in the legal system, particularly in generating victim impact statements, are mentioned and provide context to the article.
- **Gary Marchant**
    - A professor of law, ethics and emerging technologies at Arizona State University.
    - Gary Marchant's views on the ethical and legal implications of using AI in creating false videos or statements in court provide additional context to the article.

    - The incident that led to Christopher Pelkey's death in a road rage altercation.

    - The date of the first retrial of the case that led to Wales seeking to use AI.

## How a visit from actor Jon Voight led Trump to post about movie tariffs

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5389865)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 16:24:00-20:24_

### Summary

This article discusses President Donald Trump's announcement of a 100% tariff on movies produced outside the U.S., which led to a series of public and private discussions about the film industry's struggles and potential policy solutions. Trump's plan was met with skepticism and confusion from the film industry, and he later hedged on the plan, saying he was not looking to hurt the industry and wanting to meet with entertainment business leaders. The president met with actor Jon Voight and two business associates over the weekend at Mar-a-Lago, where Voight presented Trump with a plan to 'rescue' the American film industry with federal tax incentives, co-production treaties with other countries, and subsidies for theater owners and film and TV production companies. Trump's initial announcement came on Truth Social, which sparked public interest and speculation about the tariffs' effects on the film industry. Despite the president's assurances, the film industry remains concerned about the potential consequences of the tariffs, and the broader conversation about how to save the film industry continues.

### Key Takeaways

His suggestion of federal tax incentives, co-production treaties, and subsidies for film and TV production companies is a key element of the discussion in the article.
- **Trump**
    - President of the United States who announced a 100% tariff on movies produced outside the U.S.
    - President Trump's announcement of the tariff on foreign-produced movies triggered a significant debate in Hollywood about the film industry's struggles and potential solutions. His reaction and the subsequent discussion around his tariff plan are central to the article.
- **Truth Social**
    - Platform used by President Trump to make his announcement about the movie tariffs.
    - Truth Social was the platform through which President Trump initially announced his plan to impose a 100% tariff on foreign-produced movies, leading to the subsequent discussions about the film industry's current state and potential policy solutions.

The next voting session is scheduled for Thursday morning, with four daily voting sessions planned until a candidate achieves a two-thirds majority. The conclave, a secret process, is crucial to the Catholic Church's leadership and is eagerly watched by pilgrims, journalists, and cardinals alike.

## Trump administration plans to deport migrants to Libya, but court order blocks it

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5389739)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 19:54:00-04:00_

### Summary

The Trump administration is planning to deport migrants without legal status to Libya, a country that has a history of armed conflict and poor human rights records, according to a U.S. official. However, Libyan officials have denied any talks with the U.S. about the plans. A U.S. District Judge has ruled against any removals to Libya, stating that sending noncitizens without prior written notice and a meaningful opportunity to raise fear-based claims would violate existing court orders. The Trump administration has been seeking to deport migrants to other countries, including Latin American nations. The U.S. military would be responsible for carrying out these deportations. As part of the crackdown, the Trump administration has been working with other countries to deport migrants, including El Salvador and Colombia.

### Key Takeaways
  - The Trump administration plans to deport migrants to Libya, a country with a history of conflict and poor human rights records.

## In the wake of tariffs, cargo at the Port of LA is down 35%

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5389955)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 19:03:00.000Z_

### Summary

The article discusses how the Port of LA and Long Beach experienced a 35% drop in cargo volume, with a total of 19.9 million containers handled last year. This decrease, attributed to increased tariffs against Chinese goods, impacts a broad range of industries including trucking, shipping, and distribution centers. The immediate impact is felt by the dock workers and independent salesmen who are seeing a significant drop in their sales. The executive director of the Port of LA, Gene Seroka, highlights the long-term implications, suggesting that decades-old trade patterns might be permanently altered, potentially leading to a shift in trade patterns with countries like China. Diane Middleton, a former harbor commissioner, also emphasized the potential for supply chain disruptions and increased prices for consumers. Overall, the decrease in cargo volume has created uncertainty and economic hardship for a significant portion of the Southern California economy.

### Key Takeaways
  - The Port of LA and Long Beach experienced a 35% drop in cargo volume compared to the same week last year, affecting various industries and businesses.
  - The impact extends beyond the immediate area, affecting the economy of Los Angeles, Long Beach, and potentially across the entire U.S.
  - The drop in cargo volume, due to increased tariffs, could lead to shortages and higher prices for certain goods within the next four to six weeks.

    - People who work loading and unloading shipping containers at the Port of LA.

    - An independent salesman who sells gloves and safety gear to port workers.

- **Rob Walpole**
    - CEO of Customs Goods, a company handling product shipments at the Port of LA.

- **Gene Seroka**
    - Executive Director of the Port of LA.
    - He provides a comprehensive overview of the port's impact on the city, region, and country, emphasizing the long-term implications of reduced cargo volumes.
- **Diane Middleton**
    - Former Los Angeles City Harbor Commissioner.
    - She offers insights into the long-term effects of the decrease in cargo volume, suggesting that trade patterns may be permanently altered.

## Disney's newest theme park will be in Abu Dhabi

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5389601)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 15:14:00-20:14_

### Summary

Development on Yas Island has been ongoing for less than two decades, and the new park will join existing theme parks on the island, including those developed by Miral. The Walt Disney Company's statement emphasizes the cultural compatibility of the park with Abu Dhabi, framing it as a significant endorsement of the location. However, the article also notes that Disney's business practices, including its handling of anti-LGBTQ+ policies, have been subject to criticism and internal employee concerns.

## Sean 'Diddy' Combs' fame posed challenges during jury selection

- [source](https://text.npr.org/g-s1-64868)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 17:34:00-05:00_

### Summary

Judge Arun Subramanian completed the questioning of nearly 100 potential jurors for Sean 'Diddy' Combs' sex trafficking trial on Wednesday. The trial, which involves charges of sex trafficking, transporting to engage in prostitution, and racketeering conspiracy, began in the federal District Court for the Southern District of New York. The judge asked jurors about their personal experiences with topics such as sexual assault, domestic violence, and their ability to remain impartial, given the case's high profile. Potential jurors also had to answer questions about their knowledge of the allegations against Combs, including the controversial surveillance video showing him violently treating his ex-girlfriend Cassie Ventura. The trial, which is expected to last eight weeks and is scheduled to begin with opening statements on May 12, faced challenges in finding impartial jurors due to Combs' fame and the extensive media coverage of the case. Jurors who admitted to being biased against wealthy celebrities or had personal experiences with sexual assault were dismissed. Some jurors were also dismissed for other reasons such as medical exemptions, lack of English proficiency, and scheduling conflicts. By Wednesday afternoon, 45 jurors had been selected to move forward, with the prosecution and defense narrowing the pool down to 12 jurors and six alternates for the trial.

### Key Takeaways
  - Judge Arun Subramanian questioned nearly 100 potential jurors for Sean Combs' trial on sexual trafficking charges.

### Named Entities
- **Sean 'Diddy' Combs**
    - The accused rapper, producer, and businessman who faces sex trafficking charges.
    - Combs' high profile case, involving sex trafficking charges and civil lawsuits, makes it challenging to find impartial jurors.
- **Judge Arun Subramanian**
    - The judge overseeing the jury selection process.
    - The judge played a crucial role in questioning jurors to find impartial individuals for Combs' trial.
- **Cassie Ventura**
    - The ex-girlfriend of Sean Combs, featured in the controversial surveillance video.
    - Cassie Ventura's involvement in the trial, through the controversial video, makes it difficult to find unbiased jurors.
- **Marc Agnifilo**
    - The lead defense attorney for Sean Combs.
    - Agnifilo expressed frustration about the video's impact on the jury selection process, indicating the media exposure and public scrutiny involved.
- **NPR**
    - A news organization providing updates on the trial.
    - NPR provided context and updates on the trial process, including information about the jury selection challenges and potential jurors' experiences.

### Important Dates
  - **2025-05-07**
    - The day when jury selection for Sean Combs' sex trafficking trial ended, marking a significant part of the legal process.

### Important Timeframes

    - The time frame when jury selection is progressing, with the trial expected to begin soon after.

## How a post #MeToo law opened the floodgates for allegations against Sean 'Diddy' Combs

- [source](https://text.npr.org/g-s1-64329)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 09:47:00.000Z_

### Summary

Sean 'Diddy' Combs, a music mogul, is facing a sex trafficking and racketeering trial and numerous civil lawsuits alleging sexual and physical abuse dating back over a decade. The lawsuits began with Cassie Ventura's November 2023 lawsuit, which opened a legal window for alleged survivors to file claims. This legal window was enabled by New York's Adult Survivors Act, which allowed alleged victims of sexual violence a one-year window to file civil claims even after the statute of limitations had lapsed. The act's expiration in November 2022 coincided with a surge in civil lawsuits filed against Combs, including those from several women. The lawsuits against Combs, including Ventura's, may have prompted federal law enforcement to launch a criminal investigation, which led to his indictment on charges that mirror Ventura's allegations. Since then, several more civil lawsuits have been filed against Combs, and it is likely that some of the alleged victims will be called as witnesses during his criminal trial. The attention on the legal proceedings against Combs has raised hopes for more lookback legislation to provide more protection for alleged survivors of abuse.

### Key Takeaways
  - The expiration of New York's Adult Survivors Act in November 2022 provided a legal window for alleged survivors to file civil lawsuits against Sean 'Diddy' Combs, potentially opening the floodgates for more allegations and civil suits.
  - The civil lawsuits filed against Combs, including those by Cassie Ventura, may have prompted federal law enforcement to launch a criminal investigation against him, leading to his indictment on charges that mirror Ventura's allegations.

### Named Entities
- **Sean 'Diddy' Combs**
    - Music mogul who was the subject of the civil and criminal legal proceedings.
    - He is the central figure in the legal proceedings against him, facing a sex trafficking and racketeering trial, civil lawsuits, and a criminal investigation.
- **Cassie Ventura**
    - Ex-partner of Sean Combs who was the first to file a civil lawsuit against him.
    - She filed the first civil lawsuit against Combs, which may have sparked a series of legal actions against him, including a criminal investigation.
- **New York Adult Survivors Act**
    - 'A law that gave alleged victims of sexual violence a one-year window, from November 2022 to November 2023, to file civil claims even after the statute of limitations had lapsed.'
    - It was a key piece of legislation that allowed alleged victims of sexual violence to file civil lawsuits against Combs, potentially leading to increased legal actions against him.
- **New York City's Gender-Motivated Violence Protection Law**
    - 'Provided a two-year lookback window for alleged victims of violence committed against them because of their gender.'
    - Another piece of legislation that provided a lookback window for alleged victims to file civil lawsuits against Combs, contributing to the growing number of civil suits against him.

### Important Dates
  - **2023-11-01**
    - The date when Cassie Ventura first filed a lawsuit against Sean 'Diddy' Combs, marking a significant event that may have opened the floodgates for more allegations and civil suits.
  - **2022-11-22**
    - The date when New York's Adult Survivors Act, allowing alleged victims of sexual violence a one-year window to file civil claims, expired.
  - **2023-11-21**
    - The date when Cassie Ventura's lawsuit was filed, immediately following the expiration of New York's Adult Survivors Act.
  - **2024-10-27**
    - The date when federal law enforcement raided several of Combs' properties, coinciding with the growing number of civil lawsuits and potential criminal investigation.

### Important Timeframes
  - **From _2023-10-22_ to _2023-11-21_**
    - The timeframe when New York's Adult Survivors Act expired and immediately after, marking a significant period when allegations and civil suits increased.
  - **From _2023-11-21_ to _2024-10-27_**
    - The timeframe when federal law enforcement raided Combs' properties and the criminal investigation started, coinciding with the growing number of civil lawsuits and allegations.
  - **From _2023-11-21_ to _2025-04-26_**
    - The timeframe when the civil trials of Combs began, including the trial for which jury selection is underway.
  - **From _2023-11-21_ to _2025-05-07_**
    - The timeframe when the civil lawsuits and criminal charges against Combs reached their peak.

## What to do if you don't have a REAL ID yet, and which documents still work

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5379935)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 14:30:00-20:30_

### Summary

Starting on May 7, 2025, U.S. travelers will need a REAL ID, which requires more documentation than a standard driver's license or state ID, for domestic flights and entry into certain federal facilities. Clint Henderson, a travel editor at The Points Guy, explains that this change will occur in about a two-year window, giving airports discretion on a case-by-case basis to subject travelers to additional screening instead of requiring a REAL ID. Key points include travelers being able to bring passports or passport cards, Global Entry cards, NEXUS cards, FAST border-crossing cards, SENTRI cards, U.S. Department of Defense IDs, and enhanced driver's licenses. Tanya Broder, a representative from the National Immigration Law Center, highlights that those without legal status cannot obtain a REAL ID. While some states have been sending out enhanced driver's licenses, the new requirements may cause additional screenings and delays. This transition is part of the government's effort to enhance security and unify ID standards after 9/11 and the Oklahoma City bombing.

### Key Takeaways
  - Travelers will need a REAL ID, which requires more documentation than a standard driver's license or state ID, for domestic flights and entry into certain federal facilities starting May 7, 2025. REAL IDs will have a golden star symbol on the ID card to distinguish them from regular IDs. 
  - The transition period to the new ID requirements, allowing two years for airports to accommodate those who do not yet have a REAL ID, provides flexibility for travelers.
  - Travelers without a REAL ID can use alternative acceptable IDs such as passports, passport cards, Global Entry cards, NEXUS cards, FAST border-crossing cards, SENTRI cards, U.S. Department of Defense IDs, and enhanced driver's licenses issued by some states, as long as they meet the REAL ID requirements.
  - A two-year window exists to adapt to the new regulations and address potential logistical challenges like additional screenings and possible delays.
  - The Trump administration's rapid implementation of this law in 2017 was seen as an urgent response to security concerns after 9/11 and the Oklahoma City bombing. 

### Named Entities
- **Clint Henderson**
    - Managing editor at The Points Guy, travel magazine.
    - Provides insight and advice to travelers on how to prepare for the REAL ID requirement change, offering tips on what to bring and how to approach airport security during the transition period.
- **REAL ID**
    - A federal law requiring state identification cards to meet certain security standards.
    - The central topic of the article, discussing the implementation of the REAL ID law and its implications for travelers and immigration.
- **TSA**
    - The Transportation Security Administration, responsible for airport security.
    - The TSA is involved in the audit process and providing guidance to travelers on how to prepare for the REAL ID law implementation.
- **NEXUS**
    - An expedited entry/exit program for travelers with certain legal immigration status.
    - Explains that travelers with certain legal immigration status can obtain a REAL ID with additional documentation, but those without legal status cannot.
- **Global Entry**
    - A US Customs and Border Protection program for expedited entry into the United States.
    - Describes that travelers with Global Entry can travel without a REAL ID, highlighting the flexibility of the new ID requirements.
- **Majd Al-Waheidi**
    - The name of the editor who adapted the article for the web and edited it.
    - Part of the team that produced the radio version of the article, ensuring the article was adapted for the web.
- **Obed Manuel**
    - The name of the editor who adapted the article for the web and edited it.
    - Part of the team that produced the radio version of the article, ensuring the article was adapted for the web.
- **The Points Guy**
    - A travel magazine.
    - Provides travel tips and advice, including information on the REAL ID law and its implications for travelers.

### Important Dates
  - **2025-05-06**
    - 'The date when the article was published, marking the final update on the REAL ID law implementation, which will take effect on May 7, 2025.
  - **2022-12-31**
    - 'A reference point for the past of the Trump administration's policies, which is linked to the issue of REAL ID law implementation and its implementation timeline.
  - **2017-01-20**
    - 'The date when the Trump administration took office, linking it to the context of the REAL ID law being implemented under the current political leadership.

### Important Timeframes
  - **From _2025-04-26_ to _2025-05-06_**
    - The time frame from the publication of the article to its date of publication, highlighting the transition period between the previous and new requirements for ID documents.
