## 20 years later, the Real ID deadline is here. Here's why it took so long

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5387735)
- _Published: 2025-05-06 05:00:00.000Z_

### Summary

The article discusses the implementation of the 2005 Real ID law, which aimed to make state driver's licenses harder to counterfeit and require more information checks. Despite the law's complexities and resistance from many states, the deadline for compliance in airports is May 7, 2025. The article mentions the challenges faced by states in implementing the law, including resistance due to cost, privacy concerns, and the burden of additional documentation. It also touches on the impact of the law on immigrants, who may face additional barriers in obtaining compliant IDs. The article highlights the ongoing pushback and challenges in enforcing the Real ID Act, emphasizing the need for more time and resources to ensure compliance.

### Key Takeaways
  - The Real ID law was implemented in 2005 with the intention of making state driver's licenses harder to counterfeit and requiring more checks for the information on the cards. However, the implementation was complicated and faced resistance from many states due to cost, privacy concerns, and the burden of additional documentation. The law has led to a variety of 'flavors' of Real ID across states, with some states offering compliant licenses and others requiring additional steps for verification. The deadline for compliance in airports is May 7, 2025, affecting millions of U.S. citizens and immigrants.
  - Brian Zimmer
  - 'Brian Zimmer' is relevant as a researcher who has provided insights into the implementation of the Real ID Act, and his perspective and history with the law add context to the article's discussion on its implementation and challenges.

## The Fed holds interest rates steady as Trump's tariffs spark uncertainty

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5387499)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 14:09:00-20:09_

### Summary

The Federal Reserve held interest rates steady at 4.25% to 4.5% on Wednesday, as President Trump's tariffs continued to create economic uncertainty. Despite the president's repeated calls for the Fed to lower rates, the central bank maintained its benchmark borrowing rate in response to the increased inflation and growth concerns arising from the tariffs. The Fed is faced with the challenge of balancing potential inflation risks from the tariffs and the need to maintain a stable job market, which could lead to a 'bind' if tariffs push both inflation and unemployment up. Meanwhile, business surveys by the Institute for Supply Management reported widespread alarm that tariffs were disrupting supply chains and driving up prices, leading to higher prices for domestic producers.

### Key Takeaways
  - The Federal Reserve held interest rates steady at 4.25% to 4.5% to counter President Trump's tariffs that have increased uncertainty in the economy.

### Named Entities
- **Federal Reserve**
    - The central bank responsible for setting interest rates.
    - The central bank's decision to keep rates steady is the central focus of the article.
- **Jerome Powell**
    - Chair of the Federal Reserve.
    - He was the speaker quoted in the article discussing the economic outlook.
- **President Trump**
    - The U.S. President who has imposed tariffs and criticized the Fed.
    - He is the key figure driving the tariffs and the pressure on the Fed to lower rates.
- **Institute for Supply Management**
    - A business survey group that reported on industry concerns.
    - It provided industry perspectives on the impact of tariffs on supply chains and prices.
- **Social media post**
    - A post by President Trump on social media criticizing the Fed for not lowering interest rates.
    - It reflects the public pressure on the Fed from the President.

## JD Vance's half-brother advances in his uphill quest to become Cincinnati's mayor

- [source](https://text.npr.org/nx-s1-5389536)
- _Published: 2025-05-07 12:35:00-20:35_

### Summary

Cory Bowman, JD Vance's half-brother and the founding co-pastor of a local evangelical church, is running for Cincinnati mayor in a primary race. While running as a Republican, Bowman has received support from his half-brother, Vice President Biden, who served as a role model for his political aspirations. The race is unusual as it involves the first Republican candidate in 16 years and is also a nonpartisan race, with a history of Democratic mayors in Cincinnati. The race is considered challenging due to the long-standing Democratic alignment of the city's political system and the fact that it is a nonpartisan election, which makes it particularly significant for the mayor's office. Bowman's campaign focuses on issues such as money management, increasing public safety, improving infrastructure, lowering property taxes, and protecting children, including safeguarding the unborn. He is also emphasizing his ties to his roots in the city, where he believes he has the greatest memories and the best people. Despite the challenges, Bowman seems to embrace the opportunity to provide voters with a choice in the mayoral race and to bring a new perspective to the city's governance.

### Key Takeaways
  - JD Vance's half-brother, Cory Bowman, is running for Cincinnati mayor in a primary race with a Republican affiliation, facing a Democratic incumbent and a third Republican candidate.
  - Bowman, a founding co-pastor of a local evangelical church and co-owner of a coffee shop, emphasizes his focus on improving Cincinnati's infrastructure, reducing property taxes, and protecting children.
  - Bowman is inspired by his half-brother, Vice President Biden, who has been a role model for him in his political endeavors.
  - While Bowman and his primary opponent, Brian Frank, are the first Republicans to run in Cincinnati's mayoral race in 16 years, the city has not had a Republican-aligned mayor in decades.
  - The race is considered an uphill battle for Bowman, as the city has a long history of electing all-Democrat mayors, and he is the first non-Democrat to run for mayor in decades.

### Named Entities
- **JD Vance**
    - The Vice President of the United States who is Cory Bowman's half-brother.
    - JD Vance's political influence and role as a role model for his half-brother Cory Bowman, as well as the race's alignment with political parties, make him a central figure in this political story.
- **Cory Bowman**
    - JD Vance's half-brother who is running for Cincinnati mayor.
    - Bowman's candidacy and his relationship to Vice President Biden make him a significant player in this political race.
- **Aftab Pureval**
    - The Democratic-aligned incumbent running for Cincinnati mayor.
    - Bowman's race against Pureval highlights the political divisions in Cincinnati.
- **Brian Frank**
    - A Republican candidate running for Cincinnati mayor.
    - Frank's candidacy and the fact that he is the first Republican in 16 years to run for mayor in Cincinnati are key elements of the race's dynamics.
- **Kamala Harris**
    - Democratic presidential candidate who won Hamilton County in the 2020 election.
    - Her performance in Hamilton County is significant as it relates to the Democratic candidate's electoral prospects in the mayoral race.
